Let me start off by saying how awfully deceiving these reviews are! Since I'm from SF, I don't have all my "go to" spots anymore...so I took a risk on this place. I rarely get my nails "professionally" done, so this time I was "treating" myself out. Boy did that take a wrong turn!

So basically, if you haven't looked at my pic that I uploaded yet, PLEASE DO. This is how my 3 star experience went for the wrong turn. So as I was getting my pedicure, which was pretty crappy too (the polish chipped within 4 days and she did not make the skin on my feet smooth at all), the manicurist was prepping me for my gel manicure. I guess I have a high tolerance for pain because I didn't notice she had completely buffed a whole section of my skin off while she haphazardly decided to use the buffer with the really rough, crystallized texture. I actually didn't even notice until she stopped and tried to secretly blot the blood that was gushing out of my finger. Yes, I said blood. So then the girls wouldn't let me wash my hands because I was highly paranoid about getting an infection and said that they would just spray alcohol on it--which is great but I just like to know I've washed ALL the gunk off my hands. Ugh, needless to say, I'm NEVER going back and I hope I save at least some people from going through such an awful experience. <gmapID>0x80803537bce0ca81:0xca5f27291620433d<//gmapID>< text>
The Atrium Garden Inn is a wonderful place to stay. My husband and I stayed three nights to celebrate our anniversary, and although we first came as guests at the inn, we left feeling like family. There are so many intricate details in the way the inn has been remodeled and decorated that it feels like a home away from home. The owner Beth puts her heart into all that she does at the inn, which definitely includes the breakfast! She arrives at 4:30am every day to ensure that a warm and delicious homemade meal is made with the freshest ingredients and is available for guests by 7:30am. My husband and I chose to sit at the table closest to the kitchen, and as a result were able to enjoy many intellectual conversations with Beth as we ate our breakfast. Beth wants every person to feel comfortable at the inn, so if guests need anything they are welcome to ask for it. The innkeeper Michael was very helpful and thoroughly explained self check-in procedures when I called to let him know we would be running late and arrive after 8:00pm. In person he is kind and always smiling and has many stories to tell. When we forgot one of our travel pillows in the room after leaving, Helena promptly messaged us and asked us what we would like them to do with it. The inn even has a very sweet cat called Ru that greeted us when we arrived and Beth brings her dog Choco, making the place very pet friendly. Overall the experience was magnificent and we look forward to returning soon!</text>

My husband and I stayed at the Atrium for two days and loved every minute of it. The two ladies that run the place are very kind and patient, and they had great recommendations for things to do in town. The room we wrre in was called the quilt room and was very clean and cozy. < text>
I went to Bryant Automotive, first week of July in 2020, after experiencing a brake light, low fluid warning on my dashboard and after an oil change service rep saw brake fluid slowly leaking from my rear brake caliper. I was worried about losing my brakes.

I took the vehicle to Bryant and they charged approximately $25.00 to diagnose the problem. They pretty much said brake fluid was leaking from the caliper and recommended  both rear calipers be replaced, along with the brake pads. They quoted me approximately $750.00 for the job (replace rear calipers and brake pads).

I was worried about having my brakes go out on me so I reluctantly agreed for the job. I felt like this was a high price for the job. They did say it was a slow leak and I could probably drive on it, but it would eventually cause low break fluid levels. I asked if they could lower the price to $500.00 and I got an immediate no.

I'm not certain, but I remember the gentleman saying my brake fluid was dark, but afterwards I asked if the fluid was flushed and he said it wasn't. This confused me, but I could have misunderstood. Overall, they were nice, but I feel like the price was way too high. I called Les Schwab today  in Redding and they quoted me a price of approximately $525.00 for the same job, but even including putting new rotors along with the pads.

While the service was nice and Bryant was able to service me the same day, on a very busy day for them - I waited around for at least 4+ hours plus - I live out of town and was in a pickle. I would recommend Les Schwab as they have better prices if you need to get brake work done. Bryant did waive the $25.00 diagnostic fee.

I can't speak for other type of work they perform. Only what is referenced in this review. I feel somewhat buyers remorse as the offer I countered of $500 was more in line with what Schwab quoted. Anyways, I think it is important to have price transparency for customers as this is what matters, along with service, so I hope this write up helps. I'll give two stars for service, and it appears they did good work, though its only been a few days. But the price was not almost 45%-50% percent more than Schwab.< /text>

< review>
Definitely not worth your time or money. It's hard to believe they have certified technicians.

Last October I brought my truck in for a diagnosis on why my truck was misfiring. After dropping it off I was called not two hours later to tell me they were done. Instead of a real diagnosis I was simply told I needed a new engine, that I had low compression in a cylinder.

After tearing into the engine myself I found the problem, a blown AFM lifter. I replaced all of the AFM components myself and my engine has ran like new since.

Fast forward to today, I bring my vehicle in for a smog inspection. They didn't complete the inspection because I do not have CA legal catalytic converter, understandable. However when I return to pick up my truck, my driver's side door will not open. When I ask which mechanic worked on my truck they simply tell me that the mechanic is on lunch and that there is no possible way they could have broken my driver's door. My door opened and closed just fine when I dropped it off, interesting that it no longer worked when I picked it up.

Don't waste your time here.<//review>

< Text>
I know you're thinking 1 star is a bit harsh... but I will explain my rating, and maybe you'll agree with me, maybe you won't.... but here it is.

I walked into this particular location at 10:30 in the morning, with an extremely full bladder. Noticing that I was the ONLY person in the restuaunt, I waited 129 seconds for her to finish whatever task she was doing before asking "how can I help you?"

Finally I was able to very politely ask her; "I know it's against policy, but would you possibly do me a favor and let me use your restroom just this once? It's kind of an emergency.."

To which she responded, verbatim; "Actuaaalllllyyyyyyyyy, the bathrooms are for customers only...so...yeah...."

I thought about reiterating the fact that I had prefaced my request with "I know it's against your policy..."
...that's why I was asking for the favor...

But I kept my cool, and seeing as my bladder was at critical mass, I countered her rejection with a new compromise;
"Okay that's fine... can I buy a fountain drink to solidify my status as 'Customer', and then use the restroom? How much is a small soda?"
"2.50"
"Okay no problem, can I get a small Dew and the key for the restroom?"
"Actuaaalllllyyyyyyyyy I won't be able to do that..."
"May I ask why not?"
"We don't open until 11 o' clock."
I looked at my watch and it was about 10:45.

Trying desperately to locate the smallest shred of humanity in her heart I ask:
"Can I please just buy something from you? Anything? I really need to use the restroom.."
"Actuaaalllllyyyyyyyyy no..."

I incredulously asked her why she seemed so ready to help me when I walked in, if she was going to refuse the business I was offering her in exchange for the use of her restroom.
She replied to this with: "Yeah... I'm sorry but the restrooms are only for customers."

....as if she hadnt already gotten that point across..

I finally guessed that I wasn't going to recieve any semblance of customer service from her. So I mentioned to her that if she didn't want people walking in and buying things that she should probably keep the front door locked and turn off the OPEN sign in the front window... and as I was walking towards the exit SHE STARTED MIMICKING WHAT I JUST SAID UNDER HER BREATH! LIKE A 5 YEAR OLD!
When I asked for her name to include in this review, she refused to tell me.
"I'm not obligated to share that information with you, sir"
I called her again once I got back to the car and politely asked for her name and the name of her supervisor. AND SHE HUNG UP THE PHONE ON ME.

I understand adhering to your workplace policy... I even respect her diligence.... but when I offered to be a customer, I did so very politely.. despite my rising state of discomfort... just to get turned down for no reason and mocked for giving her  advice that might help people not be as confused as I was... and then refused to take responsibility for her actions by not giving me her name.

After this upsetting encounter, I went to the car to tell my girlfriend about it. I had her pose as a prospective applicant so that she could go inside and get the name of the employee in question for me...

She came back with 2 things:
1. a complaint about the way she was received. [Apparently I'm not the only one who thought she lacked manners]
and 2. a business card with the employee's name & number.....
I was extremely surprised to learn that the incredibly rude employee was none other than Jacqueline Cherry THE GENERAL MANAGER!
If this is how management treats their customers, I can't even imagine what cretins the rest of the staff must be.

I for one have had enough of this particular JJ location to last me forever. I will never EVER spend my money here. Even if I was starving and it was the last restuaunt on the planet.... purely out of principle.

You've just lost a customer for life, South- Coast Jimmy John's..... and now Google users know the exact dimensions of the pole you have jammed up your respective  anus's. I sincerely hope you lose business. You should not be managing anything with that attitude.<//Text>

<Name>Walter Macalma< /Name><text>Jersey Who? Cappriotti's what?

Being a Socal native we always hear about the east coast regional foods that "supposedly" make our 'California" lifestyle food taste like bunk. This is only from transplants who really just miss home and their comfort foods. Most will not disagree with them because most people don't travel like me, haven't been where I've been or eaten where/what I've eaten.

Their commercials may suck and their app might glitch, their site may be slow, but I'm about to get real fat up in here with OC now having 5 locations and 1 less than 10 minutes from my office. Thought they aren't open as late they do deliver and you can, call, online or app order ahead. Having done both online ordering for immediate pickup and mobile ordering en route I can say it's convenient. Pretty straight forward and easy once you've signed up online. I'm still unsure what their delivery radius is, but at any given time you'll see 4-5 cars in the lot ready. Not sure about minimum delivery either.

It's small, the dÃ©cor is traditional if you've been to JJ's before. If not it's got the marble fake grain looking tile all around with white one's up the ceiling. Nostaligic pictures and a very sterile almost Firehouse subs ness to it (if you're only from here and are into subs, you'll know what I mean). It's always got a ton of people working. It should garner quite a bit of attention from the yuppy crowd as I gets good exposure. Historically the places here didn't get much, but I really think having a mixed use shopping and food court options here stifle both. It is too small and compact to compete with the Target, Chase lots down the way. Parking is pretty bad. Service is excellent, though having only been here 3 times I can't say about their latenight. Prices are good because of value and I'll elaborate on that below.

The biggest complaint about any sandwich is going to be how soggy the bread is or did it fall apart. Neither is applicable here. The bread has a nice crust, almost French baguette-esque, It doesn't fold or break like others so holds all the fresh ingredients together. Not too much lettuce and tomatoes. Mayo isn't too heavy or too lite, but you can customize that. The club sandwhiches are a whole different story. Thick bread, but not overwhelming as all their sandwiches are pretty hefty fillings. It's really more if people want a roll or slices. The Turkey 8 inch is super solid, hearty, but light, forget about the calories because you'll probably be shocked either way. The Vito with peppers and dressing on the side is much heavier and bold, but worth it as cappicola, my favorite of the non European charcutterie, is abundant. Forget the slims it's just bread, meat and cheese, basically 90% of the whole calorie intake, not enough variance in flavors and textures to keep you interested. Do not eat the gargantuan, it's the equivalent of 2-3 sandwiches in 1, literally. It loses something in terms of flavor because it's not cohesive, just a ton of flavors.

If you learn to like this place you'll love the fact that where the JJ's originated many are open till 4am and deliver till 4am and for a solid sandwich you can see why it's got such a following. I regularly use them as a fall back when I can't find anything else near my hotel when I travel so it's an absolutely convenient pleasure to have something I consider comfort food as a traveler near my work and hopefully creeping down to my home in SD.</text><user_id>109815267831202318650<//user_id><Time>1449567728487</Time>< Gmap_id>

<Date>1584671255599< /Date><text>This place has a special place in my foodie heart because it's technically my first Michelin-rated restaurant and I got to share it with my close friends that have never had dim sum before. When I first told them about it and that it was at the Del Amo Mall, they looked at me with an odd look, but trusted my judgement and are now hooked on dim sum. What I like about this place is that you're able to get some high quality dim sum without having to break the bank. It's a little bit of wait, but it's affordable and delicious! I recommend making reservations or using the Yelp app to secure your place in line.

They are known for their soup dumplings (Xiao Long Bao), but everything else is also done very well too. If you never had dim sum before, I recommend getting a variety of dumplings including wontons in spicy sauce, pot stickers, steamed buns, and their soup dumplings of course. It's easy to share and you'll figure out what you will like best. Dim sum is kind of like the Asian version of tapas, but is geared towards morning/afternoon and is usually accompanied with hot tea. Hope you like this place as much as I do!</text><userid>110545043251394065521< /userid>< Rate>

< review>
Hidden gem inside a mall. If you go during dinner time there is a wait we were quoted a 45-65 min wait but actual time was about 35. You check in to get your name on the list and you give your phone number. You receive one text letting you know your in the system and the second text they send you check in get a menu and are seated within 10ish minutes. Even though there was a wait you can tell that they have a system down to move people along.<//review>

<Review>If you haven't heard about this, please check it out.  Asian dumplings pushed farther than I've ever seen! Even a dumpling with soup on the inside (lord knows how). Dishes that you've never seen before can be hard to choose from, but the helpful staff guides you through the menu and makes suggestions--even when eating at the bar.  Tip: if you are a small party with no children, skip the wait list like business travelers do: ask the hostess if you can eat at the bar.< /Review>< Pics>

< username>
James Wan<//username>
< Time>
1579574783632< /Time>
<Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
You will never see Chinese food at the mall the same ever again after eating here.

There are no heat lamps, chaffing trays, or a worker passing out free samples here. Din Tai Fung as a corporate chain now brings to the mall gourmet fine dining delicacies at fine dining prices to boot.

Famous are the juicy pork/soup dumplings that have claimed fame. Xie Long Bao is what we are talking about and Din Tai Fung does it the best in the market right now at an astonishing pace with teams of workers in behind a fishbowl. Of course, there are many other very tasty items on the menu also. Actually, this location like all others carries the same menu and consistency of quality and taste reign the land.

You really can't go wrong with almost all their dumpling selections, but I do tend to stay away from the seafood. Pair your meal with some noodles and string beans and you'll be satisfied.

Unfortunately, the wait times at this popular location is staggering. Expect a possible one hour wait on weekends and maybe more during certain popular hours. Also, if you aren't already aware, this is fine dining even though it is at the mall. Do expect a $30 ticket for each person if you're visiting casually, and $40 per person if you're hungry.< /Text>

Pandemic UPDATE: 9-1-20 Order curbside pickup or, starting today, they have a tent in the parking lot on the west (Hawthorne) side of the mall to dine in (see pics). Curbside pickup is the small white tent next to the dine-in tent. Place your order directly on the restaurant website since the other services take part of the restaurant's money. End Update.
Best Dim Sum in the south Bay. Arrive before you are hungry and plan on a minimum of 30-45 min wait. Can be up to 2 hours.

They will text when your table is ready so just wait in the que for the hostess in the middle. Return to the podium on the right when you get your page. Expect 10-15 min more of a wait when you return.

Hot Tip: grab an open chair at the full service bar if one is available. No wait list, just stand-up for an opening.< /Text>

< Review>
Such a treat to always stop by Din Tai Fung. This restaurant tends to be a crowdpleaser when I bring my out-of-town guests here because I've never had a bad experience and the food is always top quality. The wholesome family style eating environment is comfortable and preferred over many other similar dining spaces. The interior design of this place is really chic and interesting because the sleek black and tan design seems to be a fusion of traditional and modern Taiwanese culture. Retrofitted with a bar area, there's plenty of seating and they can host large groups easily.< /Review>

<Time>1568044173502</Time><resp>None< /resp><Pics>None< /Pics>< Name>
Mimi Lawrence< /Name>
< UserId.>
112150012568356142869<//UserId.>
<gmap_id>0x80dd4b2bbcf466fb:0x5b772d325bf8610e< /gmap_id>< text>
Ding Tai Feng is really for carb lovers, almost everything here is carbs! And that's why we never eat at any Ding Tai Feng restaurants because of gluten sensitivities and I am on low carb very often. Hubby really wanted to try this location at Del Amo in Torrance so I went along with him just this time!

We came in for a late lunch, had a couple drinks at the full bar while waiting for sister and her bf. The Hendrick's soda water and lime was a bit weak, but hubby's Grey Goose dry martini was very yummy. Menu was huge with almost all Chinese carbs items like dumplings, buns, dry noodles, wontons, noodle soups, fried rice, pot stickers, shao mai and more. They even had sweet dumplings as desserts. They do have limited vegetarian, vegan and gluten free items but they are just veggies and some rice items so they are supposed to be naturally gluten free?

After our waitress' detailed introduction of the menus, we decided on a few orders of their famous juicy kurobuta pork dumpling / xiao long bao, cod fish dumplings, kimchi & pork dumplings, shrimp & kurobuta pork pot stickers, spicy chicken wonton, sautÃ©ed mustard greens with shredded ginger, braised beef soup, chicken wonton soup, shrimp fried rice and chocolate & mochi XLB. The food was really delicious without MSG and not greasy at all. Everybody loved xiao long bao so we got more orders of just those. The other dumplings were yummy but not nearly as good as juicy pork XLB. Shrimp fried rice was the best I've ever had. I think it's better to just order XLB with soup, veggies and fried rice. That way you can have a more balanced meal than a whole bunch of different dumplings in my opinion. We had San Pellegrino and a few more Grey Goose martinis as beverages.

The service was top notch which was what we expected from an upscale Chinese restaurant. If you love dumplings you should really try Ding Tai Feng and you will enjoy it very much. For me it's a once in a long time thing cause I am still having headaches from all the gluten I ignored for this meal!</text>

The soup dumplings themselves were just shy of being salted enough, and the skins tasted a bit too much of flour. <review>I've eaten at three or four DTF locations at least, both in and out of California.  The Santa Anita Mall and Torrance locations are my local haunts.   In each location the food is always exceptional.  The staff are well-trained and always are pleasant and efficient.   The management do a fine job keeping service and food quality to high standards.

When you order try to balance your meal with one of the lighter dishes at the front of the menu.  And order a green (they're great).  The soups are all quite good, and the dumplings ... well that's why one goes.  The xiao lin bao and spicy shrimp abd pork dumplings are musts if it's your first time.

This is a very successful chain and they are unfailingly busy.  You might have to wait if you try to dine at peak times.<//review>< pics>

< text>
Finally after a month of being open, we had tried to come 4 times and every time was like 2-1/2 hour wait...  but this time we managed to come at the right time. A good time to come is during the week as soon as they open or before dinner rush. We only had to wait 5 minutes. We had spicy wontons with pork and shrimp by far my favorite dish. I could drink The flavorful sauce they serve it in mmm. Also we had bok choy and cabbage, chicken dumplings, kimchi and pork dumplings. We also had Shang high rice cakes with chicken that was my least favorite item we had ordered. This dish lacked in flavor. Love this place and can't wait to come back. Make sure every one in your party is there before you try to sit down. Store policy that every member of your party is present if you want to be seated.< /text>

<pictures>None</pictures><userid>104138211836870323044< /userid><gmap_id>0x80dd4b2bbcf466fb:0x5b772d325bf8610e</gmap_id>< time>

< review>
We came here on a super busy day (the weekend before Christmas), so the mall was very crowded, but we were seated within 10 minutes. We spent that time looking through the window in the front of the restaurant where you can watch the staff prepare fresh dumplings! It's definitely a little mesmerizing since they have a little dumpling assembly line going on, so it's nice to pass the time.

After we got seated, our server Jedi (FYI, it's not pronounced the Star Wars way) walked us through the menu and ordering process since we haven't been there before. It's basically a list of all the menu items on a sheet of paper where you indicate how many of each item you want, similar to a sushi restaurant. For anyone new to the dumpling scene, they have a menu with descriptions and photos of each item, so it makes it really easy to order.

Most of the plates come in portions that are shareable, so I would recommend trying a little bit of everything if you're there with a group. Family style worked really well for us since we all wanted to order almost everything on the menu.

I would highly recommend the Pork XiaoLongBao (steamed dumplings with a little soup in each), Sauteed String Beans with Garlic, Vegetable & Pork Wontons with Spicy Sauce, and Noodles with Sesame Sauce. YUM!

We also ordered drinks and I had what I think was called the Golden Emporer, it was an Old Fashioned type drink and was just as delicious.

Jedi was great to us and we all really enjoyed our dinner. The only reason I docked a star was because the bar was super backed up and we didn't receive our drinks until we were pretty much finished with dinner. But next time I'm in town, I'll definitely be back.< /review>

<user>101861538051466037821<//user><user_name>Abigail R.</user_name><Time>1528351505582<//Time>< Text>
Great xiao long bao, sauteed kale, beef braised noodle soup, shu mai, pork chop and fried rice.  Din Tai Fung is more expensive than your typical dim sum restaurant but you are paying for the quality of the food ,exceptional service ( which is non existent in most Chinese resturants) and ambiance. If you despise an extensive wait time like I do,  go during off peak hours early lunch or early dinner.</Text>

<Name>Arthur Fu<//Name>< Review>
Another location for a famous chain. Din Tai Fung has a lot of locations in Southern California but at last we have a convenient location for the South Bay.

Their Xao Lin Bao (Shanghai Dumplings) are what they are famous for but everything is good. My server was very attentive and friendly. I ordered Xao Lin Bao and the Shrimp with rice cakes. Too much for one person but I was by myself and finished it anyway. I just sat there and sipped Jasmine tea to finish things off.

Hint: they are usually very crowded but I went around 4 on a Saturday and only had to wait for ten minutes to get seated.< /Review>

<Rating>5< /Rating><Review>Pork XiaoLongBao soup dumplings:  Don't worry about the pronunciation, they give you a sheet to order from by quantifying the items you'd like and handing it to your server.  Pork filled dumplings with  warm broth.  Be careful!  Give time for dumplings to cool, eat in one bite because the broth will squirt out everywhere.  Perfect ratio of pork and dough with a delicious broth.   I can understand some reviewers critiquing the dumplings as "plain" but just dip in soy sauce and problem solved.

Shrimp and Pork Wontons:  This is the only reason for deduction.  The wonton dough was perfection, but the shrimp and Pork combination were not harmonious to the palate.   The design of the wonton, with the shrimp on top and pork at the bottom of dough,  just didn't mesh at all.  I would skip ordering this dish next time, but you never know until you try.

Vegetable and Pork Dumplings with Spicy Sauce:  Not even by my "white girl" terms is this spicy.  But the spicy/sweet sauce is divine.   I even smothered my other dumplings into that goodness, you may get looks, but do it!

Pear and Lychee Martini:  I am always blown away at restaurants that can craft exquisite cocktails to enjoy with their food.  The bartenders are very knowledgeful and really take the time to craft your drinks (rubbing orange peel on rim of glass and using fresh ingredients). Yes, the place does get packed but stand in line for the bar area if 21 and over to expedite your wait time.

The restaurant is huge but definitely gets filled quickly especially during peak hours of happy hour and weekends.  Received top service from everyone from the hostess, bartender,  and our server.  Clean, oh my goodness, so clean!

Price wise, I thought all of the items were reasonably priced.  I don't understand people that expect 5 star food on a 1 star budget.  I will be back without a doubt!</Review>< pics>

<Response>None</Response><Review>I dined here this past Tuesday night with a party of 5, got a # a little before 6pm and was seated at 8pm. No problem, I knew there'd be a wait, I even ate a snack before heading to the mall. I love that DTF efficiently uses technology of texting you when it's time. However, I felt slightly cheated that upon checking in, I had to wait another 15 minutes before actually getting seated. What a tease!

I had their XLB pork, XLB crab/pork, seafood stir fry noodles, fried rice, spicy wontons, green beans, and veggie bun.

I was disappointed with the lack of soup inside the XLB and the pork was bland. The XLB crab/pork was actually more on the dry side.

Seafood stir fry noodles were bland and on the greasy side that lacked seafood. The fried rice was pretty tasty and not too oily as were their signature green beans. I think the spicy wontons were my favorite part of this meal. The sauce they use was so good, that I drizzled the sauce onto the stir fry noodles.

The pork bun and veggie bun were marked incorrectly. Green dot on top stood for veggie while the red for pork. After biting into this mistake, my friend and I traded since I ordered veggie and he ordered pork. The veggie bun itself was pretty good and filled with an abundance of minced green veggies. However, I've had stomach issues since after this meal and the only thing that I ate that no one else in my group ate was the veggie bun. That may be the culprit for my frequent restroom use.

Service was so-so, the server forgot a few items on the original print-out, but later remembered and added them. The pork and veggie buns were added later. He didn't check up on us as much as we'd liked and it was difficult to wave him down.

Since this DTF location just opened about 2 weeks ago, I think they need to have a pep talk with the cooks. I'm not impressed with this location compared to their Costa Mesa, Arcadia, and Glendale locations.</Review>< username>
